For the most part, paints are translucent to semi, opaque, with the white ground visible through even the brighter values.  The paints appear to have been applied in cream consistencies with slightly raised ridges of paint pushed at the edges of forms.  There are frequent areas at the margins of the forms where the paints do not meet and leave white priming exposed.  There is some indication of faint graphite underdrawing.  The work has thin coat of glossy synthetic varnish, overall, which appears to have saturated the darker values."	"2"	"Georgia O'Keeffe (American, b.1887, d.1986)   Artist"								"Generally matte to semi-gloss paints are applied thinly over a thin, absorbent ground with the texture of the canvas contributing to the overall aesthetic of the surface only in the central, lighter values. The paints appear to have been applied as soft pastes which record ridges of brush work in the light blues and blacks.  There are many holidays or tiny interstices in the weave where applied paints skipped across, exposing white priming, beneath.  This is especially true across the lower half of the work.  Brush work generally follows the horizontal fields of color.  The work does not appear to have been varnished." (American, b.1887, d.1986)   Artist"									"996"	"1920-1921"	"Jan 01 1920   Dec 31 1921"		"Stretcher is a double bevel-faced, 3/4"" x 1 3/4"", ""American"" style, mortise and tenon, mitered corner, keyable stretcher with 8 keys extant.  The canvas is the same 2 x 2 thread, unprimed, loose-weave raw linen used for the ""Tent Door"" and ""Series 1"" paintings from 1916 to 1919.  The canvas appears to have been primed using zinc white in oil, possibly with CaCO3 amendment.  The canvas appears to have been stretched with uneven tension at the tacking nails which are blued steel and placed at regular, approx 2"" intervals.  The priming in oil is on recto and verso and covers the tacking edges and nails.  The stretched canvas is trimmed almost even with the back of the stretcher.  It would appear that Felwrath Hines treated this work in the mid- to late 1960's as the extant wood keys are held in place with an excess of low-melting point lining wax, typical of Hines' treatment of O'Keeffe paintings at the time.  The work was likely cleaned and varnished with iso-butyl methacrylate at that time, although this has not been confirmed through Hines' records at the Archives of American Art."	"2"	"Georgia O'Keeffe (American, b.1887, d.1986)   Artist"								"Stretcher is a double bevel-faced, 3/4"" x 1 3/4"", ""American"" style, mortise and tenon, mitered corner, keyable stretcher with 8 keys extant.  The canvas is the same 2 x 2 thread, unprimed, loose-weave raw linen used for the ""Tent Door"" and ""Series 1"" paintings from 1916 to 1919.  The canvas appears to have been primed using zinc white in oil, possibly with CaCO3 amendment.  The canvas appears to have been stretched with uneven tension at the tacking nails which are blued steel and placed at regular, approx 2"" intervals.  The priming in oil is on recto and verso and covers the tacking edges and nails.  The stretched canvas is trimmed almost even with the back of the stretcher.  It would appear that Felwrath Hines treated this work in the mid- to late 1960's as the extant wood keys are held in place with an excess of low-melting point lining wax, typical of Hines' treatment of O'Keeffe paintings at the time.  The work was likely cleaned and varnished with iso-butyl methacrylate at that time, although this has not been confirmed through Hines' records at the Archives of American Art."	"997"	"1920-1921"	"Jan 01 1920   Dec 31 1921"			"2"	"Georgia O'Keeffe (American, b.1887, d.1986)   Artist"									"998"	"1921"	"Jan 01 1921   Dec 31 1921"			"2"	"Georgia O'Keeffe (American, b.1887, d.1986)   Artist"									"999"	"1922"	"Jan 01 1922   Dec 31 1922"		"Paints were applied thinly in cream consistencies on the unprimed surface of the canvas.  Most paints were absorbed by the canvas and have the appearance of slightly darkened, opaque stains. Only the thicker opaque reds and some cadmium yellows are applied in a stiffer paste consistency that resulted in small ridges recording the brush hairs and raised ridges of paint at the edges of the forms.  The application of the paints resulted in the inclusion of many fine linen fibers within the paint layers, giving a somewhat felted or fuzzy appearance. The texture of the canvas contributes strongly to the appearance of the finished painted surface. There are some holidays or unpainted margins between the forms where paints do not meet or overlap.  In these areas, unprimed canvas can be easily seen.  The work has a thin, unobtrusive glossy, synthetic varnish that appears spray-applied.  DPK 09.13.06"	"2"	"Georgia O'Keeffe (American, b.1887, d.1986)   Artist"								"Paints were applied thinly in cream consistencies on the unprimed surface of the canvas.  Most paints were absorbed by the canvas and have the appearance of slightly darkened, opaque stains. Only the thicker opaque reds and some cadmium yellows are applied in a stiffer paste consistency that resulted in small ridges recording the brush hairs and raised ridges of paint at the edges of the forms.  The application of the paints resulted in the inclusion of many fine linen fibers within the paint layers, giving a somewhat felted or fuzzy appearance. The texture of the canvas contributes strongly to the appearance of the finished painted surface. There are some holidays or unpainted margins between the forms where paints do not meet or overlap.  In these areas, unprimed canvas can be easily seen.  The work has a thin, unobtrusive glossy, synthetic varnish that appears spray-applied.  DPK 09.13.06"
